# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

{"content":"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n5: //!\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n8: //!\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\n10: //! ```text\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n13: //! ```\n14: //!\n15: //! (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\n22: //! ```\n23: //!\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n26: //!\n27: //! ```text\n28: //! Perfect! I've completed the analysis of the Rust borrow checker's MIR analysis chain and created the answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**MIR Borrow Checker Components:**

1. **Entry Point**: `mir_borrowck()` - The main query entry point in `lib.rs`
2. **Root Context**: `BorrowCheckRootCtxt::do_mir_borrowck()` - Orchestrates the entire borrow checking process
3. **Region Replacement**: `replace_regions_in_mir()` - Rewrites regions to use NLL variables for flow-sensitive analysis
4. **Borrow Set Building**: `BorrowSet::build()` with the `GatherBorrows` visitor - Gathers all borrows from the MIR
5. **Type Checking**: `type_check()` - Performs MIR-level type checking and generates region constraints
6. **Liveness Analysis**: `generate()` and `trace()` - Computes which regions must be live at each CFG point via reverse depth-first search
7. **Place Conflict Detection**: `borrow_conflicts_with_place()` - Detects when borrows conflict with accesses by comparing place projections
8. **Region Inference**: `compute_regions()` - Manages region constraints and creates the RegionInferenceContext
9. **Region Solving**: `RegionInferenceContext::solve()` - Solves all region constraints via constraint propagation
10. **Two-Phase Borrow Resolution**: `check_activations()` and `TwoPhaseActivation` enum - Handles special two-phase borrow semantics

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details on files, symbols, the execution chain, and a detailed narrative explanation.
